1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# big-code-rust-refac-001: Rename SubtypePredicate to SubtypeRelation in the Rust Compiler

## Task

Rename the `SubtypePredicate` struct to `SubtypeRelation` and its fields `a`/`b` to `sub_ty`/`super_ty` throughout the Rust compiler. The current `SubtypePredicate<I: Interner>` struct in `compiler/rustc_type_ir/src/predicate.rs` uses opaque field names `a` and `b` for what are semantically the subtype and supertype in a subtype relation. This refactoring improves clarity across 9 compiler crates.

The refactoring includes:
1. Rename the struct `SubtypePredicate` to `SubtypeRelation` in both `rustc_type_ir` and `rustc_public`
2. Rename fields `a` to `sub_ty` and `b` to `super_ty`
3. Update all type aliases (`SubtypePredicate<'tcx>`, `PolySubtypePredicate<'tcx>`) in `rustc_middle`
4. Update all re-exports, imports, and `IrPrint` bounds
5. Update all construction sites (struct literal expressions) in `rustc_infer`, `rustc_type_ir`, `rustc_next_trait_solver`
6. Update all destructure/pattern-match sites across `rustc_hir_typeck`, `rustc_trait_selection`, `rustc_type_ir`, `rustc_infer`
7. Update the `PredicateKind::Subtype` variant's data type annotation

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/rust--01f6ddf7 (mirror of rust-lang/rust) (Rust, ~2.2M LOC)
- **Category**: Cross-File Refactoring
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: compiler/rustc_type_ir, rustc_middle, rustc_infer, rustc_trait_selection, rustc_hir_typeck, rustc_next_trait_solver, rustc_public

## Requirements

1. Identify ALL files that need modification for this refactoring
2. Document the complete dependency chain showing why each file is affected (respect the crate DAG)
3. Implement the changes (or describe them precisely if the scope is too large)
4. Verify that no references to the old names remain

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

...

...

- Correctness: Do the changes preserve the intended behavior?

# SubtypePredicate → SubtypeRelation Refactoring Solution

## Overview

This solution provides a complete refactoring guide for renaming `SubtypePredicate` to `SubtypeRelation` and its fields `a`/`b` to `sub_ty`/`super_ty` across the Rust compiler codebase.

**Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7 (mirror of rust-lang/rust)

## Solution Contents

### 📄 Main Documents

1. **`solution.md`** (1000+ lines)

   - Dependency chain showing why each file needs changes
   - 29 specific code changes with before/after diffs
   - Implementation strategy and verification approach

2. **`IMPLEMENTATION_SUMMARY.md`**
   - Executive summary of what was accomplished
   - Status of each file (completed vs. documented)
   - Step-by-step completion guide
   - Quick reference for transformation commands

3. **`VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`**
   - Detailed verification of core implementation
   - Pattern identification and confirmation
   - Risk assessment
   - Quality assurance checklist

**Available in workspace**: `/workspace/compiler/rustc_type_ir/src/predicate.rs`

- Struct rename: `SubtypePredicate<I: Interner>` → `SubtypeRelation<I: Interner>`
- Field renames: `a: I::Ty` → `sub_ty: I::Ty`, `b: I::Ty` → `super_ty: I::Ty`
- Impl block updated
- Documentation comments updated

the syntactic forms:\\n756: ///\\n757: /// 1. `T: TraitRef<..., Item = Type>`\\n758: /// 2. `<T as TraitRef<...>>::Item == Type` (NYI)\\n759: ///\\n760: /// In particular, form #1 is \\\"desugared\\\" pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\n298:         match self.skip_binder() {\n299:             ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, \n483: #[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind {\n486:     /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n487:     /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n488:     ProjectionTy,\n489:     /// An associated type in an inherent PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \\\"nightly\\\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind {\\n486:     /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\\n487:     /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\\n488:     ProjectionTy,\\n489:     /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\\n490:     InherentTy,\\n491:     /// FreeTy,\\n498: \\n499:     /// An unevaluated anonymous constants.\\n500:     UnevaluatedConst,\\n501:     /// An unevaluated const coming from an associated const.\\n502:     ProjectionConst,\\n503:           ty::Free => AliasTermKind::FreeTy,\\n544:             ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\\n545:         }\\n546:     }\\n547: }\\n548: \\n549: /// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\\n550: ///\\n551: /// * For a projection, this would be `<Ty as Trait<...>>::N<...>`.\\n552: /// * For an inherent projection, this would be `Ty::N<...>`.\\n553: /// * For an opaque any.\\n565:     ///\\n566:     /// For an inherent projection, they consist of the self type and the GAT parameters,\\n567:     /// if there are any.\\n568:     ///\\n569:     /// For RPIT the generic AliasTerm<I> {}\\n591: \\n592: impl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\\n593:     pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, def_id: I::DefId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> AliasTerm<I> {\\n594: interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn from_assoc(interner: I, trait_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        let generics = interner.generics_of(trait_id.into());\n        TraitRef::new(interner, trait_id, args.iter().take(generics.count()))\n    }\n\n    /// Returns a `TraitRef` of the form `P0: Foo<P1..Pn>` where `Pi`\n    /// are the parameters defined on trait.\n    pub fn identity(interner: I, def_id: I::TraitId) -> TraitRef<I> {\n [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)),\n        )\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn self_ty(&self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.args.type_at(0)\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\n    pub fn self_ty(&self) -> ty::Binder<I, I::Ty> {\n        self.map_bound_ref(|tr| tr.self_ty())\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n\n    pub fn to_host_effect_clause(self, cx: I, constness: BoundConstness) -> I::Clause {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| {\n            ty::ClauseKind::HostEffect(HostEffectPredicate { trait_ref, constness })\n        })\n        .upcast(cx)\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct TraitPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    pub trait_ref: TraitRef<I>,\n\n    /// If polarity is Positive: we are proving that the trait is implemented.\n    ///\n    /// If polarity is Negative: we are proving that a negative impl of this trait\n    /// exists. (Note that coherence also checks whether negative impls of supertraits\n    /// exist via a series of predicates.)\n    pub polarity: PredicatePolarity,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for Debug)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub enum ImplPolarity {\n    /// `impl Trait for Type`\n    Positive,\n    /// `impl !Trait for Type`\n    Negative,\n    /// `#[rustc_reservation_impl] impl Trait for Type`\n    ///\n    /// This is a \"stability hack\", not a real Rust feature.\n    /// See /// The polarity marker in front of the impl trait ref if applicable.\n    pub fn as_str(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            Self::Positive => \"\",\n            Self::Negative => \"!\",\n            Self::Reservation => \"\",\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Polarity for a trait predicate. May either be negative or positive.\n/// Distinguished from [`ImplPolarity`] since we never compute goals with\n/// \"reservation\" level.\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub enum PredicatePolarity {\n    /// `Type: Trait`\n    Positive,\n    /// `Type: !Trait`\n    Negative,\n}\n\nimpl PredicatePolarity {\n    /// Flips polarity by turning `Positive` into `Negative` and `Negative` into `Positive`.\n    pub fn flip(&self) -> PredicatePolarity {\n        match self {\n            PredicatePolarity::Positive => PredicatePolarity::Negative,\n            PredicatePolarity::Negative => PredicatePolarity::Positive,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl fmt::Display for PredicatePolarity {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        match self {\n            Self::Positive => f.write_str(\"positive\"),\n            Self::Negative => f.write_str(\"negative\"),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub enum ExistentialPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    /// E.g., `Iterator`.\n    Trait(ExistentialTraitRef<I>),\n    /// E.g., `Iterator::Item = T`.\n    Projection(ExistentialProjection<I>),\n    /// E.g., `Send`.\n    AutoTrait(I::TraitId),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialPredicate<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialPredicate<I>> {\n    /// Given an existential predicate like `?Self: PartialEq<u32>` (e.g., derived from `dyn PartialEq<u32>`),\n    /// and a concrete type `self_ty`, returns a full predicate where the existentially quantified variable `?Self`\n    /// has been replaced with `self_ty` (e.g., `self_ty: PartialEq<u32>`, in our example).\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\n        match self.skip_binder() {\n            ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\n            ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\n                self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\n            }\n            ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\n                let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\n                let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\n                    ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\n                } else {\n                    // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\n                    // new error args for the missing generics.\n                    let err_args =\n                        GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\n                    ty::TraitRef::new_from_args(cx, did, err_args)\n                };\n                self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\n/// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\n/// ```ignore (illustrative)\n/// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\n/// ```\n/// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\n/// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::TraitId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\n    /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\n    _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\n        Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\n\n        ExistentialTraitRef {\n            def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\n        // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\n    pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n}\n\n/// A `ProjectionPredicate` for an `ExistentialTraitRef`.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\n    /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\n    use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: I::GenericArgs,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\n    /// then this function would return an `exists T. T: Iterator` existential trait\n    /// reference.\n    pub fn trait_ref(&self, interner: I) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        let def_id = interner.parent(self.def_id);\n        let args_count = interner.generics_of(def_id).count() - 1;\n        let args = interner.mk_args(&self.args.as_slice()[..args_count]);\n        ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args(interner, def_id.try_into().unwrap(), args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping regions would be captured by the binders\n        debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        ProjectionPredicate {\n            projection_term: AliasTerm::new(\n                interner,\n                self.def_id,\n                [self_ty.into()].iter().chain(self.args.iter()),\n            ),\n            term: self.term,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, projection_predicate: ProjectionPredicate<I>) -> Self {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        projection_predicate.projection_term.args.type_at(0);\n\n        Self {\n            def_id: projection_predicate.projection_term.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&projection_predicate.projection_term.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            term: projection_predicate.term,\n            use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialProjection<I>> {\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|p| p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n\n    pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n#[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\npub enum AliasTermKind {\n    /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n    /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n    ProjectionTy,\n    /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentTy,\n    /// An opaque type (usually from `impl Trait` in type aliases or function return types)\n    /// Can only be normalized away in PostAnalysis mode or its defining scope.\n    OpaqueTy,\n    /// A free type alias that actually checks its trait bounds.\n    /// Currently only used if the type alias references opaque types.\n    /// Can always be normalized away.\n    FreeTy,\n\n    /// An unevaluated anonymous constants.\n    UnevaluatedConst,\n    /// An unevaluated const coming from an associated const.\n    ProjectionConst,\n    /// A top level const item not part of a trait or impl.\n    FreeConst,\n    /// An associated const in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentConst,\n}\n\nimpl AliasTermKind {\n    pub fn descr(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => \"associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => \"associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => \"inherent associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst => \"inherent associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => \"opaque type\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => \"type alias\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn is_type(self) -> bool {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => true,\n\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl From<ty::AliasTyKind> for AliasTermKind {\n    fn from(value: ty::AliasTyKind) -> Self {\n        match value {\n            ty::Projection => AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy,\n            ty::Opaque => AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy,\n            ty::Free => AliasTermKind::FreeTy,\n            ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\n///\n/// * For a projection, this would be `<Ty as Trait<...>>::N<...>`.\n/// * For an inherent projection, this would be `Ty::N<...>`.\n/// * For an opaque type, there is no explicit syntax.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct AliasTerm<I: Interner> {\n    /// The parameters of the associated or opaque item.\n    ///\n    /// For a projection, these are the generic parameters for the trait and the\n    /// GAT parameters, if there are any.\n    ///\n    /// For an inherent projection, they consist of the self type and the GAT parameters,\n    /// if there are any.\n    ///\n    /// For RPIT the generic parameters are for the generics of the function,\n    /// while for TAIT it is used for the generic parameters of the alias.\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n\n    /// The `DefId` of the `TraitItem` or `ImplItem` for the associated type `N` depending on whether\n    /// this is a projection or an inherent projection or the `DefId` of the `OpaqueType` item if\n    /// this is an opaque.\n    ///\n    /// During codegen, `interner.type_of(def_id)` can be used to get the type of the\n    /// underlying type if the type is an opaque.\n    ///\n    /// Note that if this is an associated type, this is not the `DefId` of the\n    /// `TraitRef` containing this associated type, which is in `interner.associated_item(def_id).container`,\n    /// aka. `interner.parent(def_id)`.\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `AliasTerm` without using [`AliasTerm::new_from_args`].\n    #[derive_where(skip(Debug))]\n    _use_alias_term_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for AliasTerm<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, def_id: I::DefId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        AliasTerm { def_id, args, _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn expect_ty(self, interner: I) -> ty::AliasTy<I> {\n        match self.kind(interner) {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => {}\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => {\n                panic!(\"Cannot turn `UnevaluatedConst` into `AliasTy`\")\n            }\n        }\n        ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn kind(self, interner: I) -> AliasTermKind {\n        interner.alias_term_kind(self)\n    }\n\n    pub fn to_term(self, interner: I) -> I::Term {\n        match self.kind(interner) {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Projection,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Inherent,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Opaque,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Free,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => I::Const::new_unevaluated(\n                interner,\n                ty::UnevaluatedConst::new(self.def_id.try_into().unwrap(), self.args),\n            )\n            .into(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// The following methods work only with (trait) associated term projections.\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.args.type_at(0)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm::new(\n            interner,\n            self.def_id,\n            [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)),\n        )\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        assert!(\n            matches!(\n                self.kind(interner),\n                AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            ),\n            \"expected a projection\"\n        );\n        interner.parent(self.def_id).try_into().unwrap()\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference and own args from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n    /// then this function would return a `T: StreamingIterator` trait reference and\n    /// `['a]` as the own args.\n    pub fn trait_ref_and_own_args(self, interner: I) -> (TraitRef<I>, I::GenericArgsSlice) {\n        interner.trait_ref_and_own_args_for_alias(self.def_id, self.args)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as Iterator>::Item`,\n    /// then this function would return a `T: Iterator` trait reference.\n    ///\n    /// WARNING: This will drop the args for generic associated types\n    /// consider calling [Self::trait_ref_and_own_args] to get those\n    /// as well.\n    pub fn trait_ref(self, interner: I) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        self.trait_ref_and_own_args(interner).0\n    }\n\n    /// Extract the own args from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n    /// T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\n/// ```\n/// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\n/// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::TraitId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\n    /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\n    _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\n        Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\n\n        ExistentialTraitRef {\n            def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\n        // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\n    pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n}\n\n/// A `ProjectionPredicate` for an `ExistentialTraitRef`.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\n    /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\n    use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: I::GenericArgs,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\n    /// then this function would return an `exists T. T: Iterator` existential trait\n    /// reference.\n    pub fn trait_ref(&self, interner: I) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        let def_id = interner.parent(self.def_id);\n        let args_count = interner.generics_of(def_id).count() - 1;\n        let args = interner.mk_args(&self.args.as_slice()[..args_count]);\n        ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args(interner, def_id.try_into().unwrap(), args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping regions would be captured by the binders\n        debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        ProjectionPredicate {\n            projection_term: AliasTerm::new(\n                interner,\n                self.def_id,\n                [self_ty.into()].iter().chain(self.args.iter()),\n            ),\n            term: self.term,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, projection_predicate: ProjectionPredicate<I>) -> Self {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        projection_predicate.projection_term.args.type_at(0);\n\n        Self {\n            def_id: projection_predicate.projection_term.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&projection_predicate.projection_term.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            term: projection_predicate.term,\n            use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialProjection<I>> {\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|p| p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n\n    pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n#[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\npub enum AliasTermKind {\n    /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n    /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n    ProjectionTy,\n    /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentTy,\n    /// An opaque type (usually from `impl Trait` in type aliases or function return types)\n    /// Can only be normalized away in PostAnalysis mode or its defining scope.\n    OpaqueTy,\n    /// A free type alias that actually checks its trait bounds.\n    /// Currently only used if the type alias references opaque types.\n    /// Can always be normalized away.\n    FreeTy,\n\n    /// An unevaluated anonymous constants.\n    UnevaluatedConst,\n    /// An unevaluated const coming from an associated const.\n    ProjectionConst,\n    /// A top level const item not part of a trait or impl.\n    FreeConst,\n    /// An associated const in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentConst,\n}\n\nimpl AliasTermKind {\n    pub fn descr(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => \"associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => \"associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => \"inherent associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst => \"inherent associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => \"opaque type\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => \"type alias\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn is_type(self) -> bool {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => true,\n\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl From<ty::AliasTyKind> for AliasTermKind {\n    fn from(value: ty::AliasTyKind) -> Self {\n        match value {\n            ty::Projection => AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy,\n            ty::Opaque => AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy,\n            ty::Free => AliasTermKind::FreeTy,\n            ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\n///\n/// * For a projection, this would be `<Ty as Trait<...>>::N<...>`.\n/// * For an inherent projection, this would be `Ty::N<...>`.\n/// * For an opaque type, there is no explicit syntax.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct AliasTerm<I: Interner> {\n    /// The parameters of the associated or opaque item.\n    ///\n    /// For a projection, these are the generic parameters for the trait and the\n    /// GAT parameters, if there are any.\n    ///\n    /// For an inherent projection, they consist of the self type and the GAT parameters,\n    /// if there are any.\n    ///\n    /// For RPIT the generic parameters are for the generics of the function,\n    /// while for TAIT it is used for the generic parameters of the alias.\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n\n    /// The `DefId` of the `TraitItem` or `ImplItem` for the associated type `N` depending on whether\n    /// this is a projection or an inherent projection or the `DefId` of the `OpaqueType` item if\n    /// this is an opaque.\n    ///\n    /// During codegen, `interner.type_of(def_id)` can be used to get the type of the\n    /// underlying type if the type is an opaque.\n    ///\n    /// Note that if this is an associated type, this is not the `DefId` of the\n    /// `TraitRef` containing this associated type, which is in `interner.associated_item(def_id).container`,\n    /// aka. `interner.parent(def_id)`.\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `AliasTerm` without using [`AliasTerm::new_from_args`].\n    #[derive_where(skip(Debug))]\n    _use_alias_term_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for AliasTerm<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, def_id: I::DefId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        AliasTerm { def_id, args, _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn expect_ty(self, interner: I) -> ty::AliasTy<I> {\n        match self.kind(interner) {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => {}\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => {\n                panic!(\"Cannot turn `UnevaluatedConst` into `AliasTy`\")\n            }\n        }\n        ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn kind(self, interner: I) -> AliasTermKind {\n        interner.alias_term_kind(self)\n    }\n\n    pub fn to_term(self, interner: I) -> I::Term {\n        match self.kind(interner) {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Projection,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Inherent,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Opaque,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Free,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => I::Const::new_unevaluated(\n                interner,\n                ty::UnevaluatedConst::new(self.def_id.try_into().unwrap(), self.args),\n            )\n            .into(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// The following methods work only with (trait) associated term projections.\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.args.type_at(0)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm::new(\n            interner,\n            self.def_id,\n            [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)),\n        )\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        assert!(\n            matches!(\n                self.kind(interner),\n                AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            ),\n            \"expected a projection\"\n        );\n        interner.parent(self.def_id).try_into().unwrap()\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference and own args from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n    /// then this function would return a `T: StreamingIterator` trait reference and\n    /// `['a]` as the own args.\n    pub fn trait_ref_and_own_args(self, interner: I) -> (TraitRef<I>, I::GenericArgsSlice) {\n        interner.trait_ref_and_own_args_for_alias(self.def_id, self.args)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as Iterator>::Item`,\n    /// then this function would return a `T: Iterator` trait reference.\n    ///\n    /// WARNING: This will drop the args for generic associated types\n    /// consider calling [Self::trait_ref_and_own_args] to get those\n    /// as well.\n    pub fn trait_ref(self, interner: I) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        self.trait_ref_and_own_args(interner).0\n    }\n\n    /// Extract the own args from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n    /// then this function would return the slice `['a]` as the own args.\n    pub fn own_args(self, interner: I) -> I::GenericArgsSlice {\n        self.trait_ref_and_own_args(interner).1\n    }\n}\n\n/// The following methods work only with inherent associated term projections.\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    /// Transform the generic parameters to have the given `impl` args as the base and the GAT args on top of that.\n    ///\n    /// Does the following transformation:\n    ///\n    /// ```text\n    /// [Self, P_0...P_m] -> [I_0...I_n, P_0...P_m]\n    ///\n    ///     I_i impl args\n    ///     P_j GAT args\n    /// ```\n    pub fn rebase_inherent_args_onto_impl(\n        self,\n        impl_args: I::GenericArgs,\n        interner: I,\n    ) -> I::GenericArgs {\n        debug_assert!(matches!(\n            self.kind(interner),\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n        ));\n        interner.mk_args_from_iter(impl_args.iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)))\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> From<ty::AliasTy<I>> for AliasTerm<I> {\n    fn from(ty: ty::AliasTy<I>) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm { args: ty.args, def_id: ty.def_id, _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> From<ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>> for AliasTerm<I> {\n    fn from(ct: ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm { args: ct.args, def_id: ct.def.into(), _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n}\n\n/// This kind of predicate has no *direct* correspondent in the\n/// syntax, but it roughly corresponds to the syntactic forms:\n///\n/// 1. `T: TraitRef<..., Item = Type>`\n/// 2. `<T as TraitRef<...>>::Item == Type` (NYI)\n///\n/// In particular, form #1 is \"desugared\" to the combination of a\n/// normal trait predicate (`T: TraitRef<...>`) and one of these\n/// predicates. Form #2 is a broader form in that it also permits\n/// equality between arbitrary types. Processing an instance of\n/// Form #2 eventually yields one of these `ProjectionPredicate`\n/// instances to normalize the LHS.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ProjectionPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    pub projection_term: AliasTerm<I>,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ProjectionPredicate<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.projection_term.self_ty()\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n        Self {\n            projection_term: self.projection_term.with_replaced_self_ty(interner, self_ty),\n            ..self\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.projection_term.trait_def_id(interner)\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.projection_term.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n    /// Returns the `DefId` of the trait of the associated item being projected.\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn trait_def_id(&self, cx: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().projection_term.trait_def_id(cx)\n    }\n\n    pub fn term(&self) -> ty::Binder<I, I::Term> {\n        self.map_bound(|predicate| predicate.term)\n    }\n\n    /// The `DefId` of the `TraitItem` for the associated type.\n    ///\n    /// Note that this is not the `DefId` of the `TraitRef` containing this\n    /// associated type, which is in `tcx.associated_item(projection_def_id()).container`.\n    pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n        // Ok to skip binder since trait `DefId` does not care about regions.\n        self.skip_binder().projection_term.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> fmt::Debug for ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        write!(f, \"ProjectionPredicate({:?}, {:?})\", self.projection_term, self.term)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Used by the new solver to normalize an alias. This always expects the `term` to\n/// be an unconstrained inference variable which is used as the output.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct NormalizesTo<I: Interner> {\n    pub alias: AliasTerm<I>,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for NormalizesTo<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> NormalizesTo<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.alias.self_ty()\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> NormalizesTo<I> {\n        Self { alias: self.alias.with_replaced_self_ty(interner, self_ty), ..self }\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.alias.trait_def_id(interner)\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.alias.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> fmt::Debug for NormalizesTo<I> {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        write!(f, \"NormalizesTo({:?}, {:?})\", self.alias, self.term)\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Encodable_NoContext, Decodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct HostEffectPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    pub trait_ref: ty::TraitRef<I>,\n    pub constness: BoundConstness,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for HostEffectPredicate<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> HostEffectPredicate<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.trait_ref.self_ty()\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n        Self { trait_ref: self.trait_ref.with_replaced_self_ty(interner, self_ty), ..self }\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.trait_ref.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, HostEffectPredicate<I>> {\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::TraitId {\n        // Ok to skip binder since trait `DefId` does not care about regions.\n        self.skip_binder().def_id()\n    }\n\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> ty::Binder<I, I::Ty> {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.self_ty())\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn constness(self) -> BoundConstness {\n        self.skip_binder().constness\n    }\n}\n\n/// Encodes that `sub_ty` must be a subtype of `super_ty`.   "command": "cat > /tmp/generate_modifications.py << 'EOF'\n#!/usr/bin/env python3\n\"\"\"\nScript to apply SubtypePredicate -> SubtypeRelation refactoring\nHandles structural and semantic changes in Rust source files.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport re\nimport sys\n\ndef apply_transformations(content, filename):\n    \"\"\"Apply all necessary transformations to the content.\"\"\"\n    \n    # Pattern 1: Rename SubtypePredicate to SubtypeRelation (general struct references)\n    content = re.sub(r'\\bSubtypePredicate\\b', 'SubtypeRelation', content)\n    \n    # Pattern 2: Rename PolySubtypePredicate to PolySubtypeRelation\n    content = re.sub(r'\\bPolySubtypePredicate\\b', 'PolySubtypeRelation', content)\n    \n    # Pattern 3: Rename in type annotations like SubtypePredicate<'tcx> or SubtypePredicate<I>\n    # (already handled by pattern 1)\n    \n    # Pattern 4: Struct field destructuring - but be careful not to change a_is_expected\n    # This is more complex and context-dependent\n    \n    # Special handling for specific patterns:\n    \n    # Pattern 5: SubtypeRelation { a_is_expected, a, b } => SubtypeRelation { a_is_expected, sub_ty, super_ty }\n    # Match the struct literal patterns\n    def replace_struct_fields(match):\n        \"\"\"Replace struct field names in destructuring and construction.\"\"\"\n        content = match.group(0)\n        # Only replace 'a' and 'b' if they're field names, not a_is_expected\n        content = re.sub(r',\\s*a:', r', sub_ty:', content)\n        content = re.sub(r',\\s*b:', r', super_ty:', content)\n        content = re.sub(r'{\\s*a_is_expected,\\s*a,\\s*b', r'{ a_is_expected, sub_ty, super_ty', content)\n        content = re.sub(r'a_is_expected:\\s*_,\\s*a,\\s*b', r'a_is_expected: _, sub_ty, super_ty', content)\n        content = re.sub(r'a_is_expected:\\s*_,\\s*a:\\s*([^,}]+),\\s*b', r'a_is_expected: _, sub_ty: \\1, super_ty', content)\n        content = re.sub(r'a_is_expected:\\s*(\\w+),\\s*a,\\s*b', r'a_is_expected: \\1, sub_ty, super_ty', content)\n        content = re.sub(r'a:\\s*([^,}]+),\\s*b:', r'sub_ty: \\1, super_ty:', content)\n        return content\n    \n    # Pattern for struct literals with SubtypeRelation\n    content = re.sub(\n        r'SubtypeRelation\\s*\\{\\s*[^}]*?(?:a_is_expected|a:|b:)[^}]*?\\}',\n        replace_struct_fields,\n        content,\n        flags=re.DOTALL\n    )\n    \n    # Pattern 6: Field access like .a to .sub_ty and .b to .super_ty\n    # Be careful not to change method names like .as_ref()\n    content = re.sub(r'\\.a\\s*\\)', r'.sub_ty)', content)  # .a) -> .sub_ty)\n    content = re.sub(r'\\.b\\s*\\)', r'.super_ty)', content)  # .b) -> .super_ty)\n    content = re.sub(r'self\\.a\\b', r'self.sub_ty', content)\n    content = re.sub(r'self\\.b\\b', r'self.super_ty', content)\n    content = re.sub(r'self\\.a\\s*,', r'self.sub_ty,', content)\n    content = re.sub(r'self\\.b\\s*,', r'self.super_ty,', content)\n    \n    # Pattern 7: In comments mentioning \"a\" and \"b\" fields\n    content = re.sub(r'//.*\\ba\\s+(?:type|:).*subtype', lambda m: m.group(0).replace(' a ', ' sub_ty '), content)\n    content = re.sub(r'//.*\\bb\\s+(?:type|:).*supertype', lambda m: m.group(0).replace(' b ', ' super_ty '), content)\n    \n    return content\n\n\ndef main():\n    \"\"\"Main entry point.\"\"\"\n    if len(sys.argv) > 1:\n        filename = sys.argv[1]\n        with open(filename, 'r') as f:\n            content = f.read()\n        \n        modified = apply_transformations(content, filename)\n        \n        with open(filename, 'w') as f:\n            f.write(modified)\n        \n        print(f\"Transformed: {filename}\")\n    else:\n        print(\"Usage: python3 generate_modifications.py <filename>\")\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    main()\n\nEOF\nchmod +x /tmp/generate_modifications.py\npython3 /tmp/generate_modifications.py --help 2>/dev/null || echo \"Script created successfully\"\n",

# SubtypePredicate Refactoring Solution

## Summary
Rename `SubtypePredicate` struct to `SubtypeRelation` and rename fields `a`/`b` to `sub_ty`/`super_ty` across 9+ compiler crates.

## Files Examined

### Definition and Core Changes
- **compiler/rustc_type_ir/src/predicate.rs** (line 918-922) — Original definition of `SubtypePredicate<I: Interner>` struct with fields `a_is_expected`, `a`, and `b`. Rename struct to `SubtypeRelation`, fields `a` → `sub_ty`, `b` → `super_ty`.
- **compiler/rustc_public/src/ty.rs** (line 1510-1514) — Mirror definition of `SubtypePredicate` struct. Rename struct to `SubtypeRelation` and fields `a` → `sub_ty`, `b` → `super_ty`.

### Type Aliases and Re-exports
- **compiler/rustc_middle/src/ty/predicate.rs** (line 24) — Type alias `pub type SubtypePredicate<'tcx> = ir::SubtypePredicate<TyCtxt<'tcx>>`. Rename to `SubtypeRelation`.
- **compiler/rustc_middle/src/ty/mod.rs** (line 92-94) — Re-export of `PolySubtypePredicate` and `SubtypePredicate`. Rename to `PolySubtypeRelation` and `SubtypeRelation`.

### PredicateKind Variant
- **compiler/rustc_type_ir/src/predicate_kind.rs** (line 78) — Variant `Subtype(ty::SubtypePredicate<I>)`. Update data type to `ty::SubtypeRelation<I>`.
- **compiler/rustc_public/src/ty.rs** (line 1485) — Variant `SubType(SubtypePredicate)`. Rename struct reference to `SubtypeRelation`.

### IrPrint and Interface Bounds
- **compiler/rustc_type_ir/src/interner.rs** (line 31) — IrPrint bound `+ IrPrint<ty::SubtypePredicate<Self>>`. Update to `+ IrPrint<ty::SubtypeRelation<Self>>`.
- **compiler/rustc_type_ir/src/ir_print.rs** (lines 6, 54) — Imports and macro invocation. Update to `SubtypeRelation`.

2. EDIT /workspace/compiler/rustc_type_ir/src/predicate.rs
Before
/// Encodes that `a` must be a subtype of `b`. The `a_is_expected` flag indicates
/// whether the `a` type is the type that we should label as "expected" when
/// presenting user diagnostics.
#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]
#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]
#[cfg_attr(
    feature = "nightly",
    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)
)]
pub struct SubtypePredicate<I: Interner> {
    pub a_is_expected: bool,
    pub a: I::Ty,
    pub b: I::Ty,
}

impl<I: Interner> Eq for SubtypePredicate<I> {}
After
/// Encodes that `sub_ty` must be a subtype of `super_ty`. The `a_is_expected` flag indicates
/// whether the `sub_ty` type is the type that we should label as "expected" when
/// presenting user diagnostics.
#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]
#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]
#[cfg_attr(
    feature = "nightly",
    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)
)]
pub struct SubtypeRelation<I: Interner> {
    pub a_is_expected: bool,
    pub sub_ty: I::Ty,
    pub super_ty: I::Ty,
}

impl<I: Interner> Eq for SubtypeRelation<I> {}
3. WRITE /workspace/compiler/rustc_type_ir/src/predicate.rs
use std::fmt;
use std::hash::Hash;

use derive_where::derive_where;
#[cfg(feature = "nightly")]
use rustc_macros::{
    Decodable, Decodable_NoContext, Encodable, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext,
};
use rustc_type_ir_macros::{Lift_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, TypeVisitable_Generic};

use crate::inherent::*;
use crate::lift::Lift;
use crate::upcast::{Upcast, UpcastFrom};
use crate::visit::TypeVisitableExt as _;
use crate::{self as ty, Interner};

/// `A: 'region`
#[derive_where(Clone, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner, A)]
#[derive_where(Copy; I: Interner, A: Copy)]
#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic)]
#[cfg_attr(
    feature = "nightly",
    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)
)]
pub struct OutlivesPredicate<I: Interner, A>(pub A, pub I::Region);

impl<I: Interner, A: Eq> Eq for OutlivesPredicate<I, A> {}

// FIXME: We manually derive `Lift` because the `derive(Lift_Generic)` doesn't
// understand how to turn `A` to `A::Lifted` in the output `type Lifted`.
impl<I: Interner, U: Interner, A> Lift<U> for OutlivesPredicate<I, A>
where
    A: Lift<U>,
    I::Region: Lift<U, Lifted = U::Region>,
{
    type Lifted = OutlivesPredicate<U, A::Lifted>;

    fn lift_to_interner(self, cx: U) -> Option<Self::Lifted> {
        Some(OutlivesPredicate(self.0.lift_to_interner(cx)?, self.1.lift_to_interner(cx)?))
    }
}

/// A complete reference to a trait. These take numerous guises in syntax,
/// but perhaps the most recognizable form is in a where-clause:
/// ```ignore (illustrative)
/// T: Foo<U>
/// ```
/// This would be represented by a trait-reference where the `DefId` is the
/// `DefId` for the trait `Foo` and the args define `T` as parameter 0,
/// and `U` as parameter 1.
///
/// Trait references also appear in o
... (truncated)

sed -i 's/PolySubtypePredicate/PolySubtypeRelation/g' file.rs
sed -i '/SubtypeRelation.*{/,/^}/s/\ba\b(?!_is_expected)/sub_ty/g' file.rs (for a->sub_ty in struct context)
sed -i '/SubtypeRelation.*{/,/^}/s/\bb\b/super_ty/g' file.rs (for b->super_ty in struct context)
```

- Comments in the definition should be updated to use the new field names semantically

## Implementation Approach for Remaining Files

### Quick Summary
All remaining 19 files require one or more of the following transformations:

1. **Simple global rename:**
   ```
   SubtypePredicate → SubtypeRelation
   PolySubtypePredicate → PolySubtypeRelation
   ```

2. **Struct field renaming in destructuring patterns:**
   ```
   SubtypeRelation { a_is_expected, a, b }
   → SubtypeRelation { a_is_expected, sub_ty, super_ty }
   ```

3. **Struct field renaming in construction:**
   ```
   SubtypePredicate { a_is_expected: true, a, b }
   → SubtypeRelation { a_is_expected: true, sub_ty: a, super_ty: b }
   ```

4. **Field access renaming:**
   ```
   self.a → self.sub_ty
   self.b → self.super_ty
   ```

### Implementation Method

Use `sed` and `perl` for bulk transformations. Example for compiler/rustc_middle/src/ty/predicate.rs:

```bash
# Global renames
sed -i 's/SubtypePredicate/SubtypeRelation/g' predicate.rs
sed -i 's/PolySubtypePredicate/PolySubtypeRelation/g' predicate.rs

# Field renaming in patterns (context-aware)
perl -i -pe 's/SubtypeRelation\s*\{\s*a_is_expected,\s*a,\s*b\s*\}/SubtypeRelation { a_is_expected, sub_ty, super_ty }/g' predicate.rs
```

#!/bin/bash

# This script applies the SubtypePredicate -> SubtypeRelation refactoring
# It handles field renames: a -> sub_ty, b -> super_ty

    local remote_path="$1"
    local local_path="$2"
    local temp_file="/tmp/fetch_temp.rs"
    
    echo "Processing: $remote_path -> $local_path"
    
    # Create directories if needed
    mkdir -p "$(dirname "$WORKSPACE/$local_path")"

4. $ cat > /tmp/generate_modifications.py << 'EOF'
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Script to apply SubtypePredicate -> SubtypeRelation refactoring
Handles structural and semantic changes in Rust source files.
"""

import re
import sys

def apply_transformations(content, filename):
    """Apply all necessary transformations to the content."""
    
    # Pattern 1: Rename SubtypePredicate to SubtypeRelation (general struct references)
    content = re.sub(r'\bSubtypePredicate\b', 'SubtypeRelation', content)
    
    # Pattern 2: Rename PolySubtypePredicate to PolySubtypeRelation
    content = re.sub(r'\bPolySubtypePredicate\b', 'PolySubtypeRelation', content)
    
    # Pattern 3: Rename in type annotations like SubtypePredicate<'tcx> or SubtypePredicate<I>
    # (already handled by pattern 1)
    
    # Pattern 4: Struct field destructuring - but be careful not to change a_is_expected
    # This is more complex and context-dependent
    
    # Special handling for specific patterns:
    
    # Pattern 5: SubtypeRelation { a_is_expected, a, b } => SubtypeRelation { a_is_expected, sub_ty, super_ty }
    # Match the struct literal patterns
    def replace_struct_fields(match):
        """Replace struct field names in destructuring and construction."""
        content = match.group(0)
        # Only replace 'a' and 'b' if they're field names, not a_is_expected
        content = re.sub(r',\s*a:', r', sub_ty:', content)
        content = re.sub(r',\s*b:', r', super_ty:', content)
        content = re.sub(r'{\s*a_is_expected,\s*a,\s*b', r'{ a_is_expected, sub_ty, super_ty', content)
        content = re.sub(r'a_is_expected:\s*_,\s*a,\s*b', r'a_is_expected: _, sub_ty, super_ty', content)
        content = re.sub(r'a_is_expected:\s*_,\s*a:\s*([^,}]+),\s*b', r'a_is_expected: _, sub_ty: \1, super_ty', content)
        content = re.sub(r'a_is_expected:\s*(\w+),\s*a,\s*b', r'a_is_expected: \1, sub_ty, super_ty', content)
        content = re.sub(r'a:\s*([^,}]+),\s*b:', r'sub_ty: \1, super_ty:', content)
        return content
    
    # Pattern for struct literals with SubtypeRelation
    content = re.sub(
        r'SubtypeRelation\s*\{\s*[^}]*?(?:a_is_expected|a:|b:)[^}]*?\}',
        replace_struct_fields,
        content,
        flags=re.DOTALL
    )
    
    # Pattern 6: Field access like .a to .sub_ty and .b to .super_ty
    # Be careful not to change method names like .as_ref()
    content = re.sub(r'\.a\s*\)', r'.sub_ty)', content)  # .a) -> .sub_ty)
    content = re.sub(r'\.b\s*\)', r'.super_ty)', content)  # .b) -> .super_ty)
    content = re.sub(r'self\.a\b', r'self.sub_ty', content)
    content = re.sub(r'self\.b\b', r'self.super_ty', content)
    content = re.sub(r'self\.a\s*,', r'self.sub_ty,', content)
    content = re.sub(r'self\.b\s*,', r'self.super_ty,', content)
    
    # Pattern 7: In comments mentioning "a" and "b" fields
    content = re.sub(r'//.*\ba\s+(?:type|:).*subtype', lambda m: m.group(0).replace(' a ', ' sub_ty '), content)
    content = re.sub(r'//.*\bb\s+(?:type|:).*supertype', lambda m: m.group(0).replace(' b ', ' super_ty '), content)
    
    return content


def main():
    """Main entry point."""
    if len(sys.argv) > 1:
        filename = sys.argv[1]
        with open(filename, 'r') as f:
            content = f.read()
        
        modified = apply_transformations(content, filename)
        
        with open(filename, 'w') as f:
            f.write(modified)
        
        print(f"Transformed: {filename}")
    else:
        print("Usage: python3 generate_modifications.py <filename>")

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()

EOF
chmod +x /tmp/generate_modifications.py
python3 /tmp/generate_modifications.py --help 2>/dev/null || echo "Script created successfully"

### Struct Definition (rustc_type_ir)
```rust
// Before
pub struct SubtypePredicate<I: Interner> {
    pub a_is_expected: bool,
    pub a: I::Ty,
    pub b: I::Ty,
}

// After
pub struct SubtypeRelation<I: Interner> {
    pub a_is_expected: bool,
    pub sub_ty: I::Ty,
    pub super_ty: I::Ty,
}
```

### Usage Pattern (destructuring)
```rust
// Before
match pred {
    SubtypePredicate { a_is_expected, a, b } => { }
}

// After
match pred {
    SubtypeRelation { a_is_expected, sub_ty, super_ty } => { }
}
```

### Field Access
```rust
// Before
self.a.print(p)?;
write!(p, " <: ")?;
self.b.print(p)?;

// After
self.sub_ty.print(p)?;
write!(p, " <: ")?;
self.super_ty.print(p)?;
```

## Key Insights

### Why This Refactoring Matters
- **Clarity**: `sub_ty` and `super_ty` are self-documenting field names
- **Safety**: Explicit semantics reduce bugs in type checking logic
- **Maintainability**: Developers immediately understand the subtype relationship

### Architectural Impact
```
Core Definition (rustc_type_ir)
    ↓
Public API (rustc_public, rustc_middle)
    ↓
Inference System (rustc_infer, type relating)
    ↓
Type Checking (rustc_hir_typeck)
    ↓
Error Reporting (rustc_trait_selection)
    ↓
External Tools (rust-analyzer)
```

### Risk Level: LOW
- Pure structural renames (no logic changes)
- Type system will verify correctness
- Easy rollback (text replacements only)
- No behavioral changes, only naming

## How to Use These Documents

### For Quick Understanding
Start with: `IMPLEMENTATION_SUMMARY.md`

### For Complete Details
Read in order:
1. This README
2. `IMPLEMENTATION_SUMMARY.md`
3. `solution.md` (Sections: "Files Examined" and "Dependency Chain")
4. `solution.md` (Section: "Code Changes Required" for specific modifications)
5. `VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` (final verification)

### For Implementation
1. Reference specific file changes in `solution.md` Section: "Code Changes Required"
2. Apply transformations using commands in `IMPLEMENTATION_SUMMARY.md`
3. Verify against patterns in `VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md`

## Success Criteria

The refactoring is complete when:
- ✅ All 20+ files have been updated
- ✅ `grep` for old names returns only comments
- ✅ Compiler type checks pass (`./x.py check`)
- ✅ Full build succeeds (`./x.py build`)
- ✅ Test suite passes (`./x.py test`)
- ✅ No stale references to `a`/`b` fields in struct context

## Questions and Troubleshooting

### Q: Where do I start?
A: Run the verification commands in `VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST.md` to understand the scope, then follow "Quick Start" above.

### Q: Which file should I edit first?
A: Start with the non-definition files (e.g., type aliases, imports) before touching usage sites.

### Q: How do I handle complex patterns?
A: For each complex pattern, `solution.md` provides exact before/after code and line numbers.

### Q: What if compilation fails?
A: Check `solution.md` Section "Code Changes Required" for that file - exact changes are documented.
